  32. There isn't anything horribly wrong with this trimmer. In fact, it does everything it is supposed to. It just doesn't do anything well.<br /><br />My main gripe is with the beard trimming guard. First, it isn't sturdy enough or shaped in the best way to guide your beard hair through the grooves and into the trimmer. When trimming my modest beard, it takes way too long because this thing will just plow over hairs, leaving them uncut. If it happens to catch the hair in the guard, the gaps in the guard teeth are so big that the hairs aren't lined up uniformly to be cut. The result is a beard with hairs of varying and non-uniform lengths. To make matters worse, the guard is only connected to the trimmer on one side and is not sturdy enough, so it will bend a little when pressed up against your face causing the trimming height to be slightly different depending on how much pressure you are applying. I trim my beard to about 1 cm or maybe slightly longer, and I use one of the highest available guard settings. If you trim your beard shorter, you may not have the same problems with the guard that I do.<br /><br />The second biggest problem is that the cutting blades on this trimmer aren't very good for trimming very short hairs. Typically, I can use a razor to shave the parts of my face where I don't keep a beard. However, in the area around my mustache and mouth, I have to use the trimmer to even up the hairs. Even when the guard is taken off, the blades on this trimmer are just too big to effectively catch and cut the shorter hairs. I have to use a second trimmer with smaller cutting blades to do that work.<br /><br />On the good side, the trimmer is priced reasonably, and it hasn't broken or malfunctioned in the several months that I have owned it. I haven't noticed it pulling hairs when I use it. It also seems to hold a charge for a reasonable length of time.<br /><br />Altogether, the trimmer tends to cut hairs unevenly and it takes a long time to do a decent job trimming your beard. I am not really happy with this trimmer and currently looking to replace it. But using this trimmer has taught me a few things to look for when shopping for a new one.

  274. Here's a concept: this tool, like all hand-held tools (and most other tools including, I would imagine, nuclear missles) takes a small learning curve to use. I took this for granted, but ... some people, maybe they don't ?<br /><br />It will do what you want it to do; just as simple as that. If you want the stubble look, it will take care of that easily, just use the lowest settings. If you want a short beard (and by this I mean as short as 4mm), it will do that. Want a somewhat fuller, 10mm (approximately) beard? It will do that; just turn to that setting and make several passes. Want a longer beard, one beyond the 10mm setting, even a big bushy beard, but groomed? Well, it will do that too, but this is where the learning curve really comes into play; a learning curve that requires YOU to use it with just a little skill. You can't just flip it on, make a pass over your face, and expect what your mental vision to happen. You have to make things happen, especially if your intent is outside the tool's settings.<br /><br />It WILL take care of the hair under the nostrils if you take the comb off and use the uncovered blade(s) with a little skill. For that matter, you can use this arrangement to trim a full bushy beard, a whole lot easier than using scissors. But you'll have to practice. In other words, this isn't necessarily a &#34;drive through, get the burger&#34; situation (what is, other than that narrow lane around Mickey D's). You have to expect to learn how to use it, which may or may not take a bit of time. I suppose some people will balk at this. Might be easier for those people to just pay a barber to do it.<br /><br />Will this tool cut? Oh yeah, does this just fine, no hair pulling. Does the charge last beyond one use? Yes; so far, much beyond. Will you be happy with it? Depends on your expectation in what you see YOUR role in the situation is. My advice is to buy it, use it, be happy if it does what you want, easily. Buy it, try it, pick up any additionalskill it take to get to where you wanted to be. You'll be better for trying it, whatever the outcome, because then you'll know more about what you're actually looking for.

  293. First let me say that if you care about the environment, you should read my final paragraph about the packaging.<br /><br />I no longer work in an office, and I hate to shave, so I decided to stop shaving recently. I wanted a device that would simply take my beard down to stubble, and this device does that fairly well. I found, however, that I had to remove the comb in order to get the closest shave. If you leave the comb on, then you have to hold the trimmer at just the right angle in order to get an even shave. With the comb off, you don't have to be so careful.<br /><br />To be honest, I used the comb only once, and it felt awkward and poorly designed. Because of that, my rating is based on using the shaver without the comb.<br /><br />With the comb off, the trimmer doesn't pull any hairs unless I pull it across my face very quickly when the hair is still long. If I shave WITH the direction of the hairs, the stubble comes out longer than if I shave against the direction. Consequently, I start out shaving with the direction of the hairs, and then end up shaving against it (to get the closest shave).<br /><br />The trimmer is fairly loud, which I don't like, but I won't go deaf from it. Also, it is light, which is nice. Somewhere in a box I have a barber's shaver made of metal. I could probably get the same kind of shave from that, but it would be fatiguing since it is heavy.<br /><br />The instructions say to clean this device after every use; but when I removed the cutting assembly after using it, I found no hairs inside. I'm sure that cleaning it once a week should be enough. Indeed, removing the cutting assembly so frequently might wear out the plastic parts.<br /><br />Overall I'm pleased with this trimmer. It's better than shaving. If you need a close shave, however, it isn't suitable. The best it can do is to give you short stubble.<br /><br />About the design: Another reviewer said that the cutters should be on the inside edge (where the curve is). At first I thought that too, but after using it a while, I realize that the cutters have to be on the outside of the curve, or you wouldn't be able to shave concave areas, like under your chin. However, the curved design of the handle isn't necessary at all. It forces me to hold the trimmer in just a certain way, which isn't the way that feels natural to me. After using the trimmer for a month or so, I've concluded that the handle would be more comfortable if it were straight.<br /><br />A small problem is that the trimmer doesn't have a light on it to tell you when the charging is finished. Actually, I see something that looks like a light, but it doesn't come on after charging, so it may not be working on my trimmer.<br /><br />Added later: I purchased an Oster T-Finisher (a real barber's tool) because I wanted my shaves to be closer, but the T-Finisher turned out to be inconvenient. It is heavy, and the cord is thick, stiff and taut, and it was much more difficult to maneuver around my face. It seems that what is needed is a product made for consumers, which means (1) cordless and (2) made of plastic so it is light. I have no doubt that the Norelco trimmer will have to be replaced more often than the Oster T-Finisher would have been, but it is worth it for the extra convenience.<br /><br />Added later: I took a star off the review because the shaver must be fully charged in order to use it. If the charge has run down, you can't just plug it into the wall and use it that way. This can prove to be a HUGE inconvenience when you need to shave before running out the door but the shaver isn't charged.<br /><br />Norelco isn't good about putting their products in environment-friendly packaging, and this device is no exception. The outer cardboard box is coated with plastic, so it isn't recyclable. Inside the box, the trimmer is wedged between a clear and a red piece of molded plastic. The pieces of plastic are recyclable and can be included with your cans and bottles, but you should recycle them separately (i.e., not attached to each other). A lot of people don't know this, but the plastic bubbles that a lot of items come in can be recycled. However, if the bubble is attached to cardboard, you must pull it off the cardboard, and then recycle them separately.<br /><br />Note: The trimmer started to malfunction after four years of use. Is four years a long time? I don't think so. Products aren't built to last any more.

It is extremely similar to the baby clipper just different color and again the height-setting system: the baby clipper is a comb which you adjust the height vertically, the QT4000 is that you rotate the circle. The blade is exactly the same.<br /><br />I bought this expecting it act like a shaver which could hold the beard so that I do not need to clean the countertop and sink every time I use it, but I am wrong. It spread the beard everywhere and I need to clean the aftermath for 5+ minutes.<br /><br />While compare with QC5530 hair clipper, this QT4000 is not good in that it is NOT WHOLE BODY WASHABLE! So it is not safe to use it in shower room. For QC5530 although it also spread all the beard, I could use it in shower room when I take shower and just flush the hair away, with this, I have to use it in front of the countertop and clean the sink with paper towel.<br /><br />The only thing good is it is small and light weight, you may consider it if you travel a lot. Otherwise, for those who want to buy this, I recommend you consider QC5530. (it is wired as I check on Amazon now QC5530 is sold for $100+..I bought it for $25 and I think it just worth this money. Anyway, any one in QC55x0 series is a good way to go).

All-in-all, a great product for the money.<br /><br />Original Review:<br />The Norelco QT4000 is a perfectly decent beard and mustache trimmer if you're looking for something that does the job without any frills.<br /><br />The design makes it difficult to get an extremely close shave but that's not what it's built for. The shortest settings gives my beard and mustache a nice scruffy look without being too long and looking ragged. The trim is even in length and the best part, for me, is that it manages to get the hair on my lower neck which my previous two trimmers always had trouble trimming.<br /><br />I've never run the trimmer down to zero charge but regularly get a week's worth of quick trims without any decline in the quality. To recharge I just plug it in when I remember and it's always ready to go the next time. There is no external light or indicator of how much charge is left but it's never been an issue.<br /><br />The charger itself is a lightweight wall plug and the cord itself is a very generous 6' (feet) in length.<br /><br />In conclusion, while there is nothing about this trimmer that makes me say, \\"Wow!\\" it's perfectly good for its price and has not failed me yet. I would not hesitate to recommend it to someone.

Also, there is no low- battery indicator, so in theory you could be halfway through a beard trim when the unit stops without warning. Then it would be 10 hours of charging before you could finish the trim job. In the meantime, let's hope you don't care about looking your best.<br /><br />Had I known these things sooner, I might have chosen a different clipper--one with replaceable batteries or one that would let me use it on an AC cord when the battery is down. However, I kept the unit and have been using it for about 6 weeks with quite satisfactory results. It's still going on its initial charge, and shows no sign of slowing down. (I have only a mustache and goatee, and I don't trim them every day.) At first it's a little tricky to reinstall the cutter blades after taking them out for cleaning, but I got the hang of it pretty quickly. Given the very reasonable price of the unit, I don't really regret buying it. Still, you might want to consider the points I make above.

  1102. A year ago I bought my guy a new hair clipper, he was very happy with the item and it worked well (he normally trims his own hair). I made the mistake of getting rid of his beard trimmer that he used (much more often) for his goatee and sideburns, I'm a girl I just assumed that these items did the same thing. After a while of hearing little digs about how \\"this would be much easier with a beard trimmer.\\" So I did my research and after looking at a few models I decided on this one. He was so happy, this model is easy and fast. It has 10 lengths that are all controlled by a dial in the middle that moves the clip up and down with simple \\"clicks\\" left or right. The clip comes off very easy, it simply pulls right out and the metal face comes off simply by pulling it out in the same manner. That makes it very easy to clean. The only thing you have to watch out for is the unit is not waterproof, you can wash the parts that you pull out but cannot run water over the unit. Nevertheless, this is a great and fast unit and it got me out of the dog house. :)

  1111. It does an acceptable but not especially impressive job of trimming. What makes the product terrible is how the battery and charging works. The instructions say to only charge the battery once it has completely run out. However, it cannot be charged while it's being used, and there's no indicator showing how much battery is left. This means that your options are to either occasionally let the battery run out while you use it (leaving you with a half trimmed beard) or disregard the instructions and shorten the life span of the battery by charging it after each use. I see no reason why they would have made this trimmer unable to run off of the power from the charging cable when the battery is dead. That is a common feature and not an expensive one to implement. And without it, this trimmer is completely unreliable.
